<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sabana_de_Bogota.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/340px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png" width="340" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/510px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sabana_de_Bogota.png/680px-Sabana_de_Bogota.png 2x" data-file-width="1068" data-file-height="902" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sabana_de_Bogota.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Bogotá savanna is the high plateau in the Andes where Bogotá is located. The flatlands are clearly visible in the topography and the result of a <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> lake; Lake Humboldt, that existed until around 30,000 years BP</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Bogotá</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span></span>/</a></span></span>¸, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[boɣoˈta]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1.ogg" title="File:Bogotá.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ca/Bogot%C3%A1.ogg" class="internal" title="Bogotá.ogg">listen</a>)</small>), officially <b>Bogotá, Distrito Capital</b>, abbreviated <b>Bogotá, D.C</b> (during the time of Spanish rule, and also from 1991 to 2000, called Santafé de Bogotá) is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> administered as the Capital District, although often thought of as part of <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Bogotá is a territorial entity of the first order, with the same administrative status as the <a href="/wiki/Department_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department (Colombia)">departments of Colombia</a>. It is the political, economic, administrative, industrial, artistic, cultural, and sports center of the country.</p>
<p>The city is located in the centre of Colombia, on a high plateau known as the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogotá savanna">Bogotá savanna</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Colombia)">Eastern Cordillera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>. It is the second-highest capital in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>), at an average of 2,640 metres (8,660&#160;ft) above sea level. Subdivided into 20 localities, Bogotá has an area of 1,587 square kilometres (613 square miles) and a relatively fresh climate that is constant over the year.</p>
<p>Bogotá was founded as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a> on August 6, 1538 by Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada</a> after a harsh <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">expedition into the Andes conquering the Muisca</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a> were the indigenous inhabitants of the region and called the settlement where Bogotá was founded <i>Bacatá</i>. After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Boyac%C3%A1" title="Battle of Boyacá">Battle of Boyacá</a> on August 7, 1819, Bogotá became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Colombian Declaration of Independence">independent</a> nation of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>'s independence from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> and during the formation of the present Colombia, Bogotá remained the capital of this territory.</p>
<p>The city is home to senior agencies of the executive branch (<a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">Office of the President</a>), the legislative branch (<a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress of Colombia</a>) and the judicial branch (<a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_Colombia" title="Supreme Court of Justice of Colombia">Supreme Court of Justice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Colombia" title="Constitutional Court of Colombia">Constitutional Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_(Colombia)" title="Council of State (Colombia)">Council of State</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Council_of_Judicature" title="Superior Council of Judicature">Superior Council of Judicature</a>). Bogotá stands out for its economic strength and associated financial maturity, its attractiveness to global companies and the quality of human capital; it is the largest business platform of Colombia where most high-impact ventures occur.<sup id="cite_ref-Hotspots_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hotspots-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheTalentIssue_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheTalentIssue-12">[12]</a></sup> The capital hosts the main market of Colombia and the <a href="/wiki/Andean_natural_region" title="Andean natural region">Andean natural region</a>, and the leading destination for new projects of foreign direct investment coming into Latin America and Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-investmentIBM_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investmentIBM-13">[13]</a></sup> It has the highest nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in the country, contributing most to the national total (24.7%), and it is the seventh-largest city by size of GDP in Latin America (about USD 159,850 million);<sup id="cite_ref-rankingsgdp_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rankingsgdp-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The airport of the city, <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_mythology" title="Muisca mythology">mythical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a></i>, has the largest volume of cargo transported in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and is third in number of people.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It is the city of Colombia with the largest number of universities and research centers,<sup id="cite_ref-TheTalentIssue_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheTalentIssue-12">[12]</a></sup> and has an important cultural offer, which is represented in many museums, of which the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogotá">Museo del Oro</a> is the most important, theaters and libraries. Bogotá ranks 52th on the Global Cities Index 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and is considered a global city type "Beta" by <a href="/wiki/GaWC" class="mw-redirect" title="GaWC">GaWC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/220px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/330px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg/440px-Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paramo_de_sumapaz_Bogota_D._C.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_Paramo" title="Sumapaz Paramo">Sumapaz Paramo</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/220px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/330px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG/440px-Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cerros_a_la_altura_de_la_calle_Setenta.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Eastern hills</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá is located in the southeasterm part of the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogotá savanna">Bogotá savanna</a> (<i>Sabana de Bogotá</i>) at an average altitude of 2,640 metres (8,660&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcaldia_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcaldia-4">[4]</a></sup> The Bogotá savanna is popularly called "<a href="/wiki/Savannah" class="mw-redirect" title="Savannah">savannah</a>" (<i>sabana</i>), but constitutes actually a <a href="/wiki/High_plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="High plateau">high plateau</a> in the Andes mountains, part of an extended region known as the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a>, which literally means "high plateau of Cundinamarca and Boyacá".</p>
<p>In the extreme south of Bogota's District, the world's largest continuous <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1ramo" title="Páramo">paramo</a> ecosystem can be found; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sumapaz_paramo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sumapaz paramo (page does not exist)">Sumapaz paramo</a> in the locality <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz" title="Sumapaz">Sumapaz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogotá River">Bogotá River</a> running NE-SW crosses the <i>sabana</i>, forming <a href="/wiki/Tequendama_Falls" title="Tequendama Falls">Tequendama Falls</a> (<i>Salto del Tequendama</i>) to the south. Tributary rivers form valleys with flourishing villages, whose economy is based on agriculture, livestock raising and artisanal production.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <i>sabana</i> is bordered to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Oriental, Colombia">Eastern Cordillera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> mountain range. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Hills_(Bogot%C3%A1)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eastern Hills (Bogotá) (page does not exist)">Eastern Hills</a>, which limit city growth, run from south to north, and form east of the centre the Guadalupe and <a href="/wiki/Monserrate" title="Monserrate">Monserrate</a> mountains. The western city limit is the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogotá River">Bogotá River</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_Paramo" title="Sumapaz Paramo">Sumapaz Paramo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Moorland" title="Moorland">moorland</a>) borders the south and to the north Bogotá extends over the plateau up to the towns of <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%ADa,_Cundinamarca" title="Chía, Cundinamarca">Chía</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sop%C3%B3" title="Sopó">Sopó</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hail_in_Bogota.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/220px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/330px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Hail_in_Bogota.jpg/440px-Hail_in_Bogota.jpg 2x" data-file-width="603" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hail_in_Bogota.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">Hailstorm</a> in Bogotá</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá has a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical highland climate">subtropical highland climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cwb</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Climate-Data.org_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-Data.org-19">[19]</a></sup> The average temperature is 14.5&#160;°C (58&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and it varies from 6 to 19&#160;°C (43 to 66&#160;°F) in fair skies days, to 10 to 18&#160;°C (50 to 64&#160;°F) in heavy rain days. Dry and rainy seasons alternate throughout the year. The driest months are December, January, July and August. The warmest month is March, bringing a maximum of 19.7&#160;°C (67.5&#160;°F). The coolest nights occur in January, with an average of 7.6&#160;°C (45.7&#160;°F) in the city; fog is very usual in early morning, 220 days per year,<sup id="cite_ref-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS-21">[21]</a></sup> whilst clear sky sunny full days are quite unusual.<sup id="cite_ref-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUNNY_AND_FOGGY_DAYS-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The official highest temperature recorded within the city limits is 30.0&#160;°C (86&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-climate_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-22">[22]</a></sup> and the lowest temperature recorded is −7.1&#160;°C (19&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-climate_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rainiest months are April, May, September, October and November, in which typical days are mostly <a href="/wiki/Overcast" title="Overcast">overcast</a>, with low clouds and some winds, bringing maximum temperatures of 18&#160;°C (64&#160;°F) and lows of 7&#160;°C (45&#160;°F).</p>
<p><br /></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_layout_and_nomenclature">Urban layout and nomenclature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Urban layout and nomenclature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/220px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png" width="220" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/330px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png/440px-How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png 2x" data-file-width="721" data-file-height="909" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:How-Bogota-Streets-are-Numbered-and-Named.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street arrangement of Bogotá based on the Cartesian coordinate system: North is to the right</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá has 20 localities, or districts, forming an extensive network of neighborhoods. Areas of higher economic status tend to be located to the north and northeast, close to the foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Oriental, Colombia">Eastern Cordillera</a>. Poorer neighborhoods are located to the south and southeast, many of them <a href="/wiki/Squatter" class="mw-redirect" title="Squatter">squatter</a> areas. The middle classes usually inhabit the central, western and northwestern sections of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The urban layout in the center of the city is based on the focal point of a square or plaza, typical of Spanish-founded settlements, but the layout gradually becomes more modern in outlying neighborhoods. The current types of roads are classified as <i>calles</i> (streets), which run perpendicular to the Cordillera, with street numbers increasing towards the north, and also towards the south (with the suffix "Sur") from Calle 0. <i>Carreras</i> (roads) run parallel to the hills, with numbering increasing as one travels east or west of Carrera 1 (with the suffix "Este" for roads east of Carrera 0). At the southeast of the city, the addresses are logically <i>sur-este</i>. Other types of roads more common in newer parts of the city may be termed <i>Eje</i> (Axis), <i>Diagonal</i> or <i>Transversal</i>. The numbering system for street addresses recently changed, and numbers are assigned according to street rank from main avenues to smaller avenues and local streets. Some of Bogotá's main roads, which also go by a proper name in addition to a number, are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Norte-Quito-Sur or NQS (North Quito South Avenue, from 9th road at north following railway to 30th road Avenue, or Quito City Avenue, and Southern Highway)</li>
<li>Autopista Norte-Avenida Caracas (Northern Highway, or 45th road, joined to Caracas Avenue, or 14th road)</li>
<li>Avenida Circunvalar (from downtown following hillside on eastern hills going to <a href="/wiki/La_Calera,_Cundinamarca" title="La Calera, Cundinamarca">La Calera</a>, mostly the 1-este (1st-east))</li>
<li>Avenida Suba (60th transversal from 100th street to the Suba Hills; 145th street from Suba Hills westward)</li>
<li>Avenida El Dorado (El Dorado Avenue, or 26th street)</li>
<li>Avenida de las Américas (Avenue of the Americas, from 34th street at east to 6th street at west)</li>
<li>Avenida Primero de Mayo (May First Avenue, or 22nd (partly 20th too) south street)</li>
<li>Avenida Ciudad de Cali (Cali City Avenue, or 86th road)</li>
<li>Avenida Boyacá (Boyacá Avenue, or 72nd road)</li>
<li>Autopista Sur (Southern Highway)</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="History of Bogotá">History of Bogotá</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bogot%C3%A1_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Bogotá history">Timeline of Bogotá history</a></div>
<p>The area of modern Bogotá was first populated by groups of indigenous people who migrated south based on the relation with the other Chibcha languages; the Bogotá savanna was the southernmost Chibcha-speaking group that exists from Nicaragua to the Andes in Colombia. The civilisation built by the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>, who settled in the valleys and fertile highlands of and surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyacá Department">Boyacá</a> and small parts of <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a>), was one of the four great civilisations in the Americas. The name <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a> has been given to a loose egalitarian society of various chiefs (<i>caciques</i>) who lived in small settlements of maximum 100 <i><a href="/wiki/Muisca_architecture" title="Muisca architecture">bohíos</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_agriculture" title="Muisca agriculture">agriculture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_economy#Salt" title="Muisca economy">salt-based</a> society of the people was rich in goldworking, <a href="/wiki/Muisca_economy#Trade" title="Muisca economy">trade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_mummification" title="Muisca mummification">mummification</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_religion" title="Muisca religion">religion</a> of the Muisca consisted of various gods, mostly related to natural phenomena as the Sun (<a href="/wiki/Su%C3%A9" title="Sué">Sué</a>) and his wife, the Moon; <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%ADa_(goddess)" title="Chía (goddess)">Chía</a>, rain <a href="/wiki/Chibchacum" title="Chibchacum">Chibchacum</a>, rainbow <a href="/wiki/Cuchavira" title="Cuchavira">Cuchavira</a> and with building and feasting (<a href="/wiki/Nencatacoa" title="Nencatacoa">Nencatacoa</a>) and wisdom (<a href="/wiki/Bochica" title="Bochica">Bochica</a>). Their complex <a href="/wiki/Muisca_calendar" title="Muisca calendar">luni-solar calendar</a>, deciphered by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Arturo_Izquierdo_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Manuel Arturo Izquierdo Peña">Manuel Izquierdo</a> based on work by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Domingo_Duquesne" title="José Domingo Duquesne">Duquesne</a>, followed three different sets of years, where the <a href="/wiki/Sidereal_year" title="Sidereal year">sidereal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synodic" class="mw-redirect" title="Synodic">synodic</a> months were represented. Their <a href="/wiki/Muisca_astronomy" title="Muisca astronomy">astronomical knowledge</a> is represented in one of the few extant landmarks of the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_architecture" title="Muisca architecture">architecture</a> of the Muisca in <i><a href="/wiki/El_Infiernito" title="El Infiernito">El Infiernito</a></i> outside <a href="/wiki/Villa_de_Leyva" title="Villa de Leyva">Villa de Leyva</a> to the north of Bogotá.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a></div>

<div class="thumbcaption">

The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada</a>, founder of the city</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chorro_quevedo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/235px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg" width="235" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/353px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Chorro_quevedo.jpg/470px-Chorro_quevedo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chorro_quevedo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The fountain of Quevedo on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chorro_de_Quevedo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chorro de Quevedo (page does not exist)">Chorro de Quevedo</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorro_de_Quevedo" class="extiw" title="es:Chorro de Quevedo">es</a>)</span>, one of the possible foundation sites of Bogotá</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first populations inhabiting the present-day <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Metropolitan Area of Bogotá">Metropolitan Area of Bogotá</a>, were hunter-gatherer people in the late Pleistocene. The oldest dated evidence thus far has been discovered in <i><a href="/wiki/El_Abra" title="El Abra">El Abra</a></i> (12,500 BP), north of <a href="/wiki/Zipaquir%C3%A1" title="Zipaquirá">Zipaquirá</a>. Slightly later dated excavations in a rock shelter southwest of the city in <a href="/wiki/Soacha" title="Soacha">Soacha</a> provided ages of ~11,000 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tequendama" title="Tequendama">Tequendama</a>. Since around 0 AD, the Muisca domesticated <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">guinea pigs</a>, part of their meat diet.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The people inhabiting the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_savanna" title="Bogotá savanna">Bogotá savanna</a> in the late 15th century were the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>, speaking <i><a href="/wiki/Chibcha_language" title="Chibcha language">Muysccubun</a></i>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Chibcha_language#Comparison_to_other_Chibchan_languages" title="Chibcha language">Chibcha</a> language family.<sup id="cite_ref-ElCarnero_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElCarnero-24">[24]</a></sup> Muisca means "people" or "person", making "Muisca people", how they are called, a <a href="/wiki/Tautology_(grammar)" title="Tautology (grammar)">tautology</a>. At the arrival of the conquerors, the population was estimated to be half a million indigenous people on the Bogotá savanna of up to two million in the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a>. They occupied the highland and mild climate flanks between the <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_Paramo" title="Sumapaz Paramo">Sumapaz Mountains</a> to the southwest and Cocuy's snowy peak to the northeast, covering an approximate area of 25,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (9,653&#160;sq&#160;mi), comprising Bogotá's high plain, the current <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyacá Department">Boyacá</a> department portion and a small <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a> region.</p>
<p>Trade was the most important activity of the Muisca with other Chibcha-speaking neighbours,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Guane_people" title="Guane people">Guane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lache_people" title="Lache people">Lache</a> and <a href="/wiki/U%27wa_people" title="U'wa people">U'wa</a> and with Cariban groups as the <a href="/wiki/Muzo_people" title="Muzo people">Muzo</a> or "Emerald People". Their knowledge of salt production from brines, a task exclusively for the <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Muisca_society" title="Women in Muisca society">Muisca women</a>, gave them the name "Salt People".<sup id="cite_ref-Daza_2728_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daza_2728-26">[26]</a></sup> Tropical fruits that didn't grow on the cool highlands, <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">coca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> were traded at markets that took place every Muisca week; every four days. At these frequent markets, the Muisca obtained various luxury goods that seem worthless in modern sense and precious metals and gemstones that seem valuable to us became abundant and used for various purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_warfare" title="Muisca warfare">Muisca warrior elite</a> was allowed to wear feathered crowns, from parrots and macacs whose habitat was to the east of the Andes; the <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawkan</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Guayupe_people" title="Guayupe people">Guayupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tegua_people" title="Tegua people">Tegua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Achagua_people" title="Achagua people">Achagua</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Muisca_cuisine" title="Muisca cuisine">Muisca cuisine</a> consisted of a stable and varied diet of <a href="/wiki/Tubers" class="mw-redirect" title="Tubers">tubers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a> and fruits. <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Maize</a> was the main ingredient of the Muisca, cultivated on <a href="/wiki/Muisca_agriculture" title="Muisca agriculture">elevated and irrigated terraces</a>. In Muysccubun exist many words for <i>maize</i>, <i>corn</i> and <a href="/wiki/Muisca_cuisine" title="Muisca cuisine">the various types and forms of it</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Daza_2728_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daza_2728-26">[26]</a></sup> The product was also the base for <a href="/wiki/Chicha#Colombia" title="Chicha">chicha</a>; the alcoholic beverage of the people, still sold in central Bogotá today. It was the drink for construction of houses, celebrations of harvests and sowing, ritual practices around the various sacred sites of the Altiplano, <a href="/wiki/Muisca_music" title="Muisca music">music and dances</a>, trade at special ferias with farther away trading indigenous groups of Colombia and to inaugurate the new highest regarded member of the community; <i>zipas</i>, <i>zaques</i>, <i>caciques</i> and the religious ruler <i><a href="/wiki/Iraca" title="Iraca">iraca</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Sun_Temple_(Sogamoso)" title="Sun Temple (Sogamoso)">Sacred City of the Sun</a> <a href="/wiki/Sogamoso" title="Sogamoso">Sugamuxi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>zipa</i> at the moment of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest</a> was <a href="/wiki/Tisquesusa" title="Tisquesusa">Tisquesusa</a>. His main <i>bohío</i> was in <i>Bacatá</i> with others in <a href="/wiki/Funza" title="Funza">Funza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cajic%C3%A1" title="Cajicá">Cajicá</a>, giving name to the present day capital of Colombia. A prophecy in his life came true; <i>he would be dying, bathing in his own blood</i>. Defending Funza with a reduced army of <a href="/wiki/Muisca_warfare" title="Muisca warfare">guecha warriors</a> against the heavily exhausted but heavily armed strangers, his reign fell in the hands of Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada and his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_P%C3%A9rez_de_Quesada" title="Hernán Pérez de Quesada">Hernán Pérez</a> on April 20, 1537. Upon his death, his brother <a href="/wiki/Sagipa" title="Sagipa">Sagipa</a> became the last <i>zipa</i>, against the <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Muisca_society" title="Women in Muisca society">inheritance tradition of the Muisca</a>. Sagipa used to be a main captain for Tisquesusa but quickly submitted to the Spanish rulers. The first <a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomenderos</a> asked high prices in valuable products and agricultural production from the indigenous people. On top of that various epidemics of European viruses razed through the population, of which in current <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyacá Department">Boyacá</a> 65-85&#160;% of the Muisca were killed within 100 years.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bogotá was founded by <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada</a> traditionally on the 6th of August 1538. Other documents state a second establishment was done on April 27, 1539. Gonzalo Jiménez and main conquerors <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_Belalc%C3%A1zar" title="Sebastián de Belalcázar">De Belalcázar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Federmann" title="Nikolaus Federmann">Federmann</a>, left for Spain in April 1539, founding <a href="/wiki/Guataqu%C3%AD" title="Guataquí">Guataquí</a> together on April 6, 1539. The rule over the fresh <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a> was left to Hernán. Bogotá became the capital of the later <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ElCarnero_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElCarnero-24">[24]</a></sup> With independence, Bogotá became capital of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> and later the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gonzalo_Jim.C3.A9nez_de_Quesada_expedition">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada expedition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada expedition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest of the Muisca</a></div>
<p>From 1533, a belief persisted that the Río Grande de la <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena</a> was the trail to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">South Sea</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, legendary <i><a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a></i>. Such was the target of <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Granada">Granadanian</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_conquistadors_in_Colombia" title="List of conquistadors in Colombia">conquistador</a> who left <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> on 6 April 1536 with 800 soldiers, heading towards the interior of current <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. The expedition divided into two groups, one under Quesada's command to move on land, and the other commanded by Diego de Urbino would go up river in four brigantine ships to, later on, meet Quesada troops at the site named Tora de las Barrancas Bermejas. When they arrived, they heard news about Indians inhabiting the south and making large salt cakes used to trade for wild cotton and fish. Jiménez decided to abandon the route to <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and cross the mountain in search of salt villages. They saw crops, trails, white salt cakes and then huts where they found corn, yucca and beans. From Tora, the expedition went up the Opón River and found indigenous people covered with very finely painted cotton mantles. When they arrived in Muisca territories, of the expedition leaving <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a>, only 162 men were left.<sup id="cite_ref-BancoList_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BancoList-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonisation">Spanish colonisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Spanish colonisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the other side to <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bolívar Square">Plaza de Bolívar</a>, the Chapter and the Royal Audience were located. The street joining the Major Plaza and Herbs Plaza —currently Santander Park— was named <i>Calle Real</i> (Royal Street), now <i>Carrera Séptima</i> (or "Seventh Street"; counted from the mountains to the east of the city).</p>
<p>Formed by Europeans, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a>, indigenous people, and slaves, from the second half of the 16th century, the population began to grow rapidly. The 1789 census recorded 18,161 inhabitants, and by 1819 the city population reached 30,000 inhabitants distributed in 195 blocks. Importance grew when the <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">Diocese</a> was established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The city mayor and the chapter formed by two councilmen, assisted by the constable and the police chief, governed the city. For better administration of these domains, in April 1550, the Audience of Santafé de Bogotá was organized. At that time, the city became the capital and the home of New Kingdom of Granada government. Fourteen years later in 1564, the Spanish Crown designated the first Royal Audience chairman, Andrés Díaz Venero de Leyva.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nineteenth_century">Nineteenth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Nineteenth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/235px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg" width="235" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/353px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg/470px-CatedralPrimadaBogota2004-7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bolívar Square">Bolívar Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/235px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg" width="235" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/353px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg/470px-Calle_real_de_Bogot%C3%A1_en_1869_dibujo_de_Therond.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1228" data-file-height="864" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The Royal Street, today known as the Seventh Avenue (Carrera Séptima)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg/235px-Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg" width="235" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg/353px-Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg/470px-Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1665" data-file-height="1135" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estacion_Sabana_1930.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogotá's Railroad Central Station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Political uneasiness felt all over Spanish colonies in America was expressed in New Granada in many different ways, accelerating the movement to independence. One of the most transcendent was the Revolution of Comuneros, a riot of the inhabitants started in Villa del Socorro —current Department of <a href="/wiki/Santander_Department" title="Santander Department">Santander</a>—in March 1781.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Spanish authorities suppressed the riot, and José Antonio Galán, the leader was executed. He left an imprint, though. He was followed in 1794 by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Antonio Nariño">Antonio Nariño</a>, precursor of independence by translating and publishing in Santa Fe, the Rights of Men and the Citizen, and by 20 July movement leaders in 1810.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Between 1819 and 1849, there were no fundamental structural changes from the colonial period. By the mid-19th century, a series of fundamental reforms were enacted, some of the most important being slavery abolition and religious, teaching, print and speech industry and trade freedom, among others.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During the decade of the 70s, radicalism accelerated reforms and state and social institutions were substantially modified. However, during the second half of the century, the country faced permanent pronouncements, declarations of rebellions between states, and factions which resulted in civil wars: the last and bloodiest was the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Days%27_War" title="Thousand Days' War">Thousand Days' War</a> from 1899 to 1902.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1823, a few years after the formation of Gran Colombia, the Public Library, now the National Library, was enlarged and modernized with new volumes and better facilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The National Museum was founded. Those institutions were of great importance to the new republic's cultural development. The Central University was the first State school, precursor of the current <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University</a>, founded in 1867 and domiciled in Bogotá.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regeneration">Regeneration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Regeneration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>President Rafael Núñez declared the end of Federalism, and in 1886 the country became a centralist republic ruled by the constitution in force – save some amendments – up to 1981. In the middle of political and administration avatars, Bogotá continued as the capital and principal political center of the country.</p>
<p>From a base of only 20,000 people in 1793, the city grew to approximately 117,000 people in 1912. Population growth was rapid after 1870, largely because of emigration from the eastern highlands.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twentieth_century">Twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Early in the 20th century, Colombia had to face devastating consequences from the One Thousand Days War, which lasted from 1899 to 1902, and the loss of <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Between 1904 and 1909, the lawfulness of the liberal party was re-established and President Rafael Reyes endeavored to implement a national government. Peace and state reorganization generated the increase of economic activities. Bogotá started deep architectural and urban transformation with significant industrial and artisan production increases.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1910, the Industrial Exposition of the Century took place at Park of Independence. Stands built evidenced industrial, artisan work, beaux arts, electricity and machinery progress achieved. The period from 1910 to 1930 is designated conservative hegemony.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Between 1924 and 1928, hard union struggles began, with oil fields and banana zone workers' strikes, leaving numerous people dead.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Bogotá had practically no industry. Production was basically artisan work grouped in specific places, similar to commercial sectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bolívar Square">Plaza de Bolívar</a> and surroundings lodged hat stores, at Calle del Comercio –current Carrera Seventh– and Calle Florián –now Carrera Eight– luxurious stores selling imported products opened their doors; at Pasaje Hernández, tailor's shops provided their services, and between 1870 and 1883, four main banks opened their doors: Bogotá, Colombia, Popular and Mortgage Credit banks.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/220px-Bogotazo.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/330px-Bogotazo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="391" data-file-height="244" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogotazo</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bogotazo" title="Bogotazo">Bogotazo</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Violencia" title="La Violencia">La Violencia</a></div>
<p>Following the banana zone killings and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Conservative_Party" title="Colombian Conservative Party">conservative party</a> division, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Olaya_Herrera" title="Enrique Olaya Herrera">Enrique Olaya Herrera</a> took office in 1930. The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Liberal_Party" title="Colombian Liberal Party">liberal party</a> reformed during 16 years of the so-called Liberal Republic, agricultural, social, political, labor, educational, economic and administrative sectors. Unionism strengthened and education coverage expanded.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The celebration produced a large number of infrastructure works, new construction and work sources. Following the 1946 liberal party division, a conservative candidate took presidential office again in 1948, after the killing of liberal leader <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Eli%C3%A9cer_Gait%C3%A1n" title="Jorge Eliécer Gaitán">Jorge Eliécer Gaitán</a>, Bogotá's downtown was virtually destroyed as violence reigned. From then, Bogotá's urban, architectural and population sectors were substantially reorganized.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The largest and most populous city in Colombia, Bogotá had 6,778,691 inhabitants within the city's limits (2005 census),<sup id="cite_ref-2005_Census_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005_Census-7">[7]</a></sup> with a population density of approximately 4,310 inhabitants per square kilometer. Only 15,810 people are located in rural areas of Capital District. 47.5% of the population are male and 52.5% women.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_(Medium_Variant).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/220px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/330px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png/440px-Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_%28Medium_Variant%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1576" data-file-height="863" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_Future_Population_(Medium_Variant).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogotá Future Population (Medium Variant)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Bogotá, as in the rest of the country, urbanization has accelerated due to industrialization as well as complex political and social reasons such as poverty and violence, which led to migration from rural to urban areas throughout the twentieth and twenty-first centuries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A dramatic example of this is the number of displaced people who have arrived in Bogotá due to the internal armed conflict.</p>
<p>Some estimates show that Bogotá's <a href="/wiki/Floating_population" title="Floating population">floating population</a> may be as high as 4 million people, most of them being migrant workers from other departments and displaced people.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The majority of the displaced population lives in the <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Bol%C3%ADvar_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciudad Bolívar (Bogotá)">Ciudad Bolívar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennedy (Bogotá)">Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usme" title="Usme">Usme</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bosa_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosa (Bogotá)">Bosa</a> sections.</p>
<p>The ethnic composition of the city’s population includes minorities of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Colombian">Afro-Colombian</a> people (1.5%), and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Indigenous Amerindians</a> (0.2%); 98.27% of the population has no ethnic affiliation,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> but are <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a> and whites.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bogotá has gone to great lengths to change its formerly notorious crime rate and its image with increasing success after being considered in the 1990s to be one of the most violent cities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In 1993 there were 4,352 intentional homicides at a rate of 81 per 100,000 people;<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> in 2007 Bogotá suffered 1,401 murders at a rate of 19 per 100,000 inhabitants, and had a further reduction to 16.9 per 100,000 inhabitants in 2012 (the lowest since 1983).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> This success was mainly the result of a participatory and integrated security policy; "Comunidad Segura", that was first adopted in 1995 and continues to be enforced.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogotá is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a>, and houses the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_Colombia" title="Supreme Court of Justice of Colombia">Supreme Court of Justice</a> and the center of the executive administration as well as the residence of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">President</a> (<a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Casa de Nariño">Casa de Nariño</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> These buildings, along with the Office of the Mayor, the Lievano Palace (Palacio Liévano), are located within a few meters from each other on the <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bolívar Square">Bolívar Square</a> (Plaza de Bolívar). The square is located in the city's historical center, <a href="/wiki/La_Candelaria" title="La Candelaria">La Candelaria</a>, which features architecture in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Colonial style">Spanish Colonial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Baroque_architecture" title="Spanish Baroque architecture">Spanish Baroque</a> styles.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="List of mayors of Bogotá">Mayor of Bogotá</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_City_Council" title="Bogotá City Council">City Council</a> – both elected by popular vote – are responsible for city administration. In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Peñalosa">Enrique Peñalosa</a> was elected Mayor; his term runs from 2016 to 2019.</p>
<p>The city is divided into 20 localities: <a href="/wiki/Usaqu%C3%A9n" title="Usaquén">Usaquén</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapinero" title="Chapinero">Chapinero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Fe (Bogotá)">Santa Fe</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Cristóbal (Bogotá)">San Cristóbal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usme" title="Usme">Usme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunjuelito" title="Tunjuelito">Tunjuelito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosa_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosa (Bogotá)">Bosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennedy (Bogotá)">Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fontib%C3%B3n" title="Fontibón">Fontibón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engativ%C3%A1" title="Engativá">Engativá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suba_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Suba (Bogotá)">Suba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrios_Unidos" title="Barrios Unidos">Barrios Unidos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teusaquillo" title="Teusaquillo">Teusaquillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_M%C3%A1rtires" title="Los Mártires">Los Mártires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonio Nariño (Bogotá)">Antonio Nariño</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puente_Aranda" title="Puente Aranda">Puente Aranda</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Candelaria" title="La Candelaria">La Candelaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Uribe_Uribe,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Rafael Uribe Uribe, Bogotá">Rafael Uribe Uribe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Bol%C3%ADvar_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciudad Bolívar (Bogotá)">Ciudad Bolívar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumapaz_(Bogot%C3%A1)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sumapaz (Bogotá)">Sumapaz</a>.</p>
<p>Each of the 20 localities is governed by an administrative board elected by popular vote, made up of no fewer than seven members. The Mayor designates local mayors from candidates nominated by the respective administrative board.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" class="image" title="View of the central business district"><img alt="View of the central business district" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/800px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" width="800" height="205" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/1200px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/1600px-Panorama_del_Centro_Internacional_de_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2335" data-file-height="598" /></a></p>
<p><br />
Bogotá is the main economic and industrial centre of Colombia. The Colombian government fosters the import of capital goods, Bogotá being one of the main destinations of these imports.</p>
<p>In 2008 the World Cities Study Group and Network (GaWC) from the United Kingdom ranked Bogotá as a beta-level city, a medium ranking. Beta-level cities are important world cities that are instrumental in linking their region or state into the world economy.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1,_Nocturna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg/220px-Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg/330px-Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg/440px-Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Nocturna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5939" data-file-height="3341" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1,_Nocturna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bogotá is the 3rd largest city within city limits in South America by population</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá is responsible for 56% of the tourism that arrives to Colombia and is home 1,423 multinational companies. Bogotá also ranked highly as a global city where business is done and meetings are held. Bogotá is a growing international meetings destination.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hotels in the historical center of La Candelaria and its surrounding areas cater to lovers of culture and the arts. This area also has the bulk of hostels in the city as well. In La Candelaria, there are many museums, including the <a href="/wiki/Botero_Museum" title="Botero Museum">Botero Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogotá">Gold Museum</a>. Close to La Candelaria is the Cerro Monserrate, which you can reach by cable car or funicular. The hotels located near Ciudad Salitre are intended for visitors who make short stops in Bogotá and near El Dorado International Airport.</p>
<p>Important landmarks and tourist stops in Bogotá include the botanical garden José Celestino Mutis, La Quinta de Bolivar, the national observatory, the planetarium, Maloka, the Colpatria observation point, the observation point of La Calera, the monument of the American flags, and La Candelaria (the historical district of the city). There is also Usaquen, a colonial landmark where brunch and flea market on Sundays is a traditional activity. The city has numerous green parks and amusement parks like Salitre Magico or Mundo Aventura.</p>
<p>Green areas surrounding Bogota are perfect locations for eco-tourism and hiking activities, in the eastern mountains of the city, just a few minutes walking from main roads, there are Quebrada La vieja and Chapinero Waterfalls, two of many green spots for sightseeing and tourism with clean air.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are also several areas of the city where fine restaurants can be found. The G Zone, the T Zone and La Macarena are well known for their gastronomic offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the 2000s, major hotel chains have established in the city.</p>
