<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping_malls">Shopping malls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Shopping malls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andino,_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/180px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/270px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG/360px-Andino%2C_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2986" data-file-height="3982" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andino,_entrada_por_la_carrera_12.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Centro Andino, an upscale mall in northern Bogotá</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá's economy has been significantly boosted due to new shopping malls built within the last few years. As of December 2011, over 160 new malls are planned in addition to the existing 100 malls.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Notable malls include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centro_Andino" title="Centro Andino">Centro Andino</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centro_Mayor" title="Centro Mayor">Centro Mayor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Commercial_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Fe Commercial Center">Santafé</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Estaci%C3%B3n" title="Gran Estación">Gran Estación</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portal_de_la_80" class="mw-redirect" title="Portal de la 80">Portal de la 80</a></li>
<li><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_comercial_Tit%C3%A1n_Plaza" class="extiw" title="es:Centro comercial Titán Plaza">Titán Plaza</a></li>
<li><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Calima" class="extiw" title="es:Centro Comercial Calima">Calima</a></li>
<li><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centro_Comercial_Atlantis_Plaza" class="extiw" title="es:Centro Comercial Atlantis Plaza">Atlantis Plaza</a></li>
<li><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicentro" class="extiw" title="es:Unicentro">Unicentro</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bogota is home to <a href="/wiki/Template:Bogot%C3%A1_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Bogotá TV">several television stations</a> like <a href="/wiki/Canal_Capital" title="Canal Capital">Canal Capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citytv_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Citytv Bogotá">Citytv</a> which are local stations, <a href="/wiki/Canal_13_(Colombia)" title="Canal 13 (Colombia)">Canal 13</a> is a regional station, and is home to the national channels <a href="/wiki/Caracol_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Caracol TV">Caracol TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/RCN_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="RCN TV">RCN TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal_Uno_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal Uno (Colombia)">Canal Uno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal_Institucional" title="Canal Institucional">Canal Institucional</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%B1al_Colombia" title="Señal Colombia">Señal Colombia</a>. It has multiple satellite television services like <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telefónica">Telefónica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claro_Americas" title="Claro Americas">Claro</a> and <a href="/wiki/DirecTV" title="DirecTV">DirecTV</a> and several satellite dishes which offer hundreds of international channels, plus several exclusive channels for Bogotá.</p>
<p>In Bogota, all the major radio networks in the country are available, in both AM and FM; 70% of the FM stations offer <a href="/wiki/Radio_Data_System" title="Radio Data System">RDS service</a>. There are several newspapers, including <i><a href="/wiki/El_Tiempo_(Colombia)" title="El Tiempo (Colombia)">El Tiempo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Espectador" title="El Espectador">El Espectador</a></i>, <i>El Periódico (Colombia)|El Periódico</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Siglo" title="El Nuevo Siglo">El Nuevo Siglo</a></i>, plus economical dailies <i>La República (Colombia)|La República</i> and <i>Portafolio</i>, tabloids <i>El Espacio</i>, <i>Q'Hubo</i>, and <i>Extra</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Communist_Party" title="Colombian Communist Party">Communist Party</a>'s <i>Voz Proletaria</i>. Bogotá also offers three free newspapers, two Spanish, ADN and <a href="/wiki/Publimetro" class="mw-redirect" title="Publimetro">Publimetro</a>, and one English, The Bogota Post.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/220px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/330px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/440px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3511" data-file-height="2633" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An old house in the <a href="/wiki/Teusaquillo" title="Teusaquillo">Teusaquillo</a> locality, near downtown Bogotá (<i>Estrato 4</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Energy and sewer bills are stratified based on the location of owner's residence and income,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> with the intended purpose that wealthier branches of society subsidize the energy and sewer bills of the poorer. Bogotá is divided into six socio-economic "estratos" (strata):</p>
<ul>
<li>Estrato 1 (lowest)</li>
<li>Estrato 2 (low)</li>
<li>Estrato 3 (mid-low)</li>
<li>Estrato 4 (mid-high)</li>
<li>Estrato 5 (high)</li>
<li>Estrato 6 (highest)</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG/220px-Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG/330px-Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG/440px-Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3859" data-file-height="2573" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_biarticulado_de_TransMilenio_por_la_av._Caracas.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A biarticulated <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> bus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá's growth has placed a strain on its roads and highways, but since 1998 significant efforts to upgrade the infrastructure have been undertaken.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Private car ownership forms a major part of the congestion, in addition to taxis, buses and commercial vehicles. Buses remain the main means of mass transit. There are two bus systems: the traditional system and the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG/220px-Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG/330px-Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG/440px-Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3904" data-file-height="2929" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_bus_SITP_en_localidad_de_Los_M%C3%A1rtires.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Urban bus (SITP), part of the integrated public transport system</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trancon_Autonorte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Trancon_Autonorte.jpg/220px-Trancon_Autonorte.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Trancon_Autonorte.jpg/330px-Trancon_Autonorte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Trancon_Autonorte.jpg/440px-Trancon_Autonorte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trancon_Autonorte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Northern Highway (<i>Autopista Norte</i>) at 100th street</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The traditional system runs a variety of bus types, operated by several companies on normal streets and avenues: <i>Bus</i> (large buses), <i>Buseta</i> (medium size buses) and <i>Colectivo</i> (vans or minivans). The bigger buses were divided into two categories: <i>Ejecutivo</i>, which was originally to be a deluxe service and was not to carry standing passengers, and <i>corriente</i> or normal service. Since May 2008, all buses run as <i>corriente</i> services. Bogotá is a <a href="/wiki/Transportation_hub" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation hub">hub</a> for domestic and international bus routes. The Bogotá terminal serves routes to most cities and towns in Colombia<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and is the largest in the country. There is international service to Ecuador, Perú and Venezuela.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> 'rapid transit system' was created during <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Peñalosa">Enrique Peñalosa</a>'s mayoral term,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and is a form of <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> that has been deployed as a measure to compensate for the lack of a subway or rail system. TransMilenio combines articulated buses that operate on dedicated bus roads (busways) and smaller buses (feeders) that operate in residential areas, bringing passengers to the main grid. TransMilenio's main routes are: Caracas Avenue, Northern Highway (<i>Autopista Norte</i>), 80th Street, Americas Avenue, Jiménez Avenue, and 30th Avenue (also referred to as <i>Norte Quito Sur</i> or <i>N.Q.S.</i> for short). Routes for Suba Avenue and Southern Highway (<i>Autopista Sur</i>), the southern leg of the 30th Avenue, were opened in April 2006. The third phase of the system will cover 7th Avenue, 10th Avenue, and 26th Street (or <i>Avenida El Dorado</i>). The system is planned to cover the entire city by 2030. Although the Transmilenio carries commuters to numerous corners of the city, it is more expensive (0.60 USD or 2000 COP) than any public transport, except taxis.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG/220px-Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG/330px-Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG/440px-Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cicloruta_r%C3%ADo_Fucha_cl_13_Sur_kr_12.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Cicloruta</i> near the Fucha River</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite the city's chronic congestion, many of the ideas enacted during the Peñalosa years are regarded worldwide to be cost-effective, efficient and unique solutions. In addition to TransMilenio, the Peñalosa administration and voter-approved referenda helped to establish travel restrictions on cars with certain license plate numbers during peak hours called <a href="/wiki/Pico_y_placa" title="Pico y placa">Pico y placa</a>; 121 kilometres (75 miles) of <a href="/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa" title="Ciclovía">Ciclovía</a> on Sundays; a massive system (376&#160;km (234&#160;mi) as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) of bicycle paths and segregated lanes called <i><a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network" title="Bogotá's Bike Paths Network">ciclorrutas</a></i>; and the removal of thousands of parking spots in an attempt to make roads more pedestrian-friendly and discourage car use. <i>Ciclorrutas</i> is one of the most extensive dedicated bike path networks of any city in the world, with a total extension of 376 kilometres (234 miles). It extends from the north of the city, 170th Street, to the south, 27th Street, and from <a href="/wiki/Monserrate" title="Monserrate">Monserrate</a> on the east to the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River" title="Bogotá River">Bogotá River</a> on the west. The <i>ciclorruta</i> was started by the 1995–1998 <a href="/wiki/Antanas_Mockus" title="Antanas Mockus">Antanas Mockus</a> administration with a few kilometers, and considerably extended during the administration of Mayor Peñalosa with the development of a Bicycle Master Plan and the addition of paths hundreds of kilometers in extent.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Since the construction of the <i>ciclorruta</i> bicycle use in the city has increased, and a car free week was introduced in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-greenblog_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenblog-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/220px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/330px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/440px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3795" data-file-height="2741" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá's principal airport is <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">El Dorado International Airport</a>, west of the city's downtown. Due to its central location in Colombia and in Latin America, it is a hub for Colombia's Flagship Carrier <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines_Colombia" title="Copa Airlines Colombia">Copa Airlines Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/LAN_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="LAN Colombia">LAN Colombia</a>. It is also serviced by a number of international airlines including American, Delta, United, Jet Blue and Lufthansa. Currently the national airport has begun to take more responsibility due to the congestion at the international airport. In response to the high demand of approximately 27 Million passengers per year,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> a new airport, El Dorado II, is planned to be built by 2021, to help alleviate traffic at the main airport.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>A secondary airport, <a href="/wiki/Military_Transport_Air_Command_(Colombian_Air_Force)" title="Military Transport Air Command (Colombian Air Force)">CATAM</a>, serves as a base for Military and Police Aviation. This airport, which uses the runways of El Dorado will eventually move to Madrid, a nearby town in the region of Cundinamarca, leaving further space to expand El Dorado.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Guaymaral_Airport" title="Guaymaral Airport">Guaymaral Airport</a> is another small airport located in the northern boundaries of Bogota. It is used mainly for private aviation activities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_and_suburban_railways">Urban and suburban railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Urban and suburban railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro" title="Bogotá Metro">Bogotá Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tramways_of_Bogot%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Tramways of Bogotá">Tramways of Bogotá</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Savannah_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogotá's Savannah Railway">Bogotá's Savannah Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Train_for_the_vicinities_of_the_city_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Train for the vicinities of the city of Bogotá">Train for the vicinities of the city of Bogotá</a></div>
<p>Bogotá has little railway transit infrastructure, following the collapse of the tram network, although a number of plans hope to change that. The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro" title="Bogotá Metro">Bogotá Metro</a> has been pushed forward by two successive governments, and proponents hope that construction will soon begin. Plans to construct railways in and out of the city, replacing defunct routes, have been delayed due to the pressing need for transport within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle_infrastructure">Bicycle infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bicycle infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network" title="Bogotá's Bike Paths Network">Bogotá's Bike Paths Network</a></div>
<p>Bogotá is the Colombian city with the most extensive and comprehensive network of bike paths. Bogotá’s bike paths network or Ciclorutas de Bogotá in Spanish, designed and built during the administration of Mayors <a href="/wiki/Antanas_Mockus" title="Antanas Mockus">Antanas Mockus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa" title="Enrique Peñalosa">Enrique Peñalosa</a>, is also one of the most extensive in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The network is integrated with the <a href="/wiki/TransMilenio" title="TransMilenio">TransMilenio</a> bus system which has bicycle parking facilities.</p>
<p>Bogota implemented a healthy habit called "Ciclovia" where principal highways are closed from 7:00&#160;a.m. till 2:00 pm on Sundays and public holidays; therefore, the People ride their bikes to enjoy the city as well as exercise. In the same way just on December the same activity is carried out in the night, there are some special activities such as fireworks, street theater performances, and street food just to mention a few.</p>
<p>Since the 4th of April 2016 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carrera_11&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carrera 11 (page does not exist)">carrera 11</a> has been reduced from four to three car lanes and a new bike lane (<i>cicloruta</i>) has been inaugurated.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tramway">Tramway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tramway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 December 1884, the first tramway pulled by mules was inaugurated and covered the route from <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square" title="Bolívar Square">Plaza de Bolívar</a> to Chapinero,<sup id="cite_ref-PorupRaub2009_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PorupRaub2009-60">[60]</a></sup> and in 1892, the line connecting Plaza de Bolívar and La Sabana Station started operating. The tramway ran over wooden rails and was easily derailed, so steel rails imported from England were eventually installed. In 1894, a tramway car ran the Bogotá-Chapinero line every 20 minutes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The tramway provided services until 1948, and was then replaced by buses.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bogot%C3%A1" title="List of universities in Bogotá">List of universities in Bogotá</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg/220px-Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg/330px-Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg/440px-Auditorio_Leon_de_Greiff.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2303" data-file-height="1535" /></a>

León de Greiff Hall at <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University of Colombia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_los_Andes_(3326108271).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/220px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/330px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/440px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>

Mario Laserna building in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Los_Andes_(Colombia)" title="University of Los Andes (Colombia)">University of the Andes</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG/220px-Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG/330px-Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG/440px-Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_%C3%81tico.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Centro Ático at <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Xavierian_University" title="Pontifical Xavierian University">Pontifical Xavierian University</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Known as the Athens of South America,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Bogotá has an extensive educational system of both primary and secondary schools and colleges. Due to the constant migration of people into the nation's capital, the availability of quotas for access to education offered by the State free of charge is often insufficient. The city also has a diverse system of colleges and private schools.</p>
<p>There are a number of universities, both public and private. In 2002, there were a total of 114 higher education institutions; in Bogotá there are several universities, most partially or fully accredited by the NAC (National Accreditation Council): <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Andes,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="University of the Andes, Colombia">University of the Andes, Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/District_University_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="District University of Bogotá">District University of Bogotá</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University,_Colombia" title="La Salle University, Colombia">La Salle University, Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_La_Sabana" title="University of La Sabana">University of La Sabana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Xavierian_University" title="Pontifical Xavierian University">Pontifical Xavierian University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Our Lady of the Rosary University">Our Lady of the Rosary University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Externado_de_Colombia" title="Universidad Externado de Colombia">Universidad Externado de Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_University_Nueva_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Military University Nueva Granada">Military University Nueva Granada</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_America" title="University of America">University of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Arboleda_University" title="Sergio Arboleda University">Sergio Arboleda University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Tadeo_Lozano_University" title="Jorge Tadeo Lozano University">Jorge Tadeo Lozano University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilot_University_of_Colombia" title="Pilot University of Colombia">Pilot University of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_University_of_Colombia" title="Catholic University of Colombia">Catholic University of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Aquinas_University" title="Saint Thomas Aquinas University">Saint Thomas Aquinas University</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Pedagogic_University_(Colombia)" title="National Pedagogic University (Colombia)">Universidad Pedagógica Nacional</a>.</p>
<p>The city has a University City at the National University of Colombia campus located in the traditional sector Teusaquillo. It is the largest campus in Colombia and one of the largest in Latin America.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/220px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/330px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/440px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ciclovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciclovia">Ciclovia</a> in Bogotá</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bogotá has many cultural venues including 58 museums, 62 art galleries, 33 library networks, 45 stage theatres, 75 sports and attraction parks, and over 150 national monuments.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Many of these are renowned globally such as: The <a href="/wiki/Luis_Angel_Arango_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Angel Arango Library">Luis Angel Arango Library</a>, the most important in the region<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> which receives well over 6 million visitors a year;<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum" title="Colombian National Museum">Colombian National Museum</a>, one of the oldest in the Americas, dating back to 1823;<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-American Theater Festival">Ibero-American Theater Festival</a>, largest of its kind in the world, receives 2 million attendees enjoying over 450 performances across theaters and off the street;<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Philharmonic" title="Bogotá Philharmonic">Bogotá Philharmonic</a> is the most important<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Symphony_orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony orchestra">symphony orchestra</a> in Colombia, with over 100 musicians and 140 performances a year;<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cristóbal Colón Theater, the country's oldest Opera House, opened in 1892. It is home to the National Symphony Association's major act, the <a href="/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_of_Colombia" title="National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia">National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rock_al_Parque" title="Rock al Parque">Rock al Parque</a> or Rock at the Park is an open air rock music festival. Recurring annually, it gathers over 320,000 music fans who can enjoy over 60 band performances for free during three days a year.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The series have been so successful during its 15 years of operation that the city has replicated the initiative for other music genres, resulting in other recent festivals like Salsa at the Park, Hip Hop at the Park, Ballet at the Park, Opera at the Park, and Jazz at the Park.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kids' Choice Awards Colombia">Kids' Choice Awards Colombia</a>, are the most important<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2015)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> awards given in the city by <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> and the first ceremony was given in 2014 by the singer <a href="/wiki/Maluma_(singer)" title="Maluma (singer)">Maluma</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Corferias" title="Corferias">Corferias</a> the ceremony has been the home of shows given by artists like <a href="/wiki/Austin_Mahone" title="Austin Mahone">Austin Mahone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pena" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Pena">Carlos Pena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Tetto" title="Don Tetto">Don Tetto</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Riva_(singer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Riva (singer) (page does not exist)">Riva</a> among others.</p>
<p>Bogotá has worked heavily in recent years to position itself as leader in cultural offerings in South America, and it is increasingly being recognized worldwide as a hub in the region for the development of the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2007, Bogotá was awarded the title of Cultural Capital of <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Ibero-America</a> by the UCCI (<a href="/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities" title="Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</a>), and it became the only city to have received the recognition twice, after being awarded for the first time in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_history">Cultural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cultural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bogotá gave the Spanish-speaking world <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Asunci%C3%B3n_Silva" title="José Asunción Silva">José Asunción Silva</a> (1865–1896), <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a> pioneer. His poetic work in the novel <i>De sobremesa</i> has a place in outstanding American literature. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Pombo" title="Rafael Pombo">Rafael Pombo</a> (1833–1912) was an <a href="/wiki/American_romanticism" class="mw-redirect" title="American romanticism">American romanticism</a> poet who left a collection of fables essential part of children imagination and Colombian tradition.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/170px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/255px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/340px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3864" data-file-height="5152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/BD_Bacat%C3%A1" title="BD Bacatá">BD Bacatá</a>, under construction, will be the city's tallest building and the second tallest in South America</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The urban morphology and typology of colonial buildings in Bogotá have been maintained since the late nineteenth century, long after the independence of Colombia (1810).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This persistence of the colonial setting is still visible, particularly in La Candelaria, the historical center of Bogotá. Also kept up are the colonial houses of two stories, with courtyards, gabled roofs, ceramic tiles and balconies. In some cases, these balconies were filled with glass during the Republican period, a distinguishing feature of the architecture of the sector (for example, the House of Rafael Pombo).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>"Republican Architecture" was the style that prevailed between 1830 and 1930.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Although there were attempts to consolidate a modern architectural language, the only examples seen are University City and White City at the National University of Colombia (constructed 1936 to 1939).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This work was developed by German architect <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Rother" title="Leopold Rother">Leopold Rother</a>, although architects of rationalist trends participated in the design of campus buildings. We also see in Bogotan architecture trends such as art deco, expressionism and organic architecture. This last trend was typified by Bogotan architects in the second half of the twentieth century such as <a href="/wiki/Rogelio_Salmona" title="Rogelio Salmona">Rogelio Salmona</a>.</p>
<p>Although renowned for its beautiful preservation of colonial architecture, there are also significant contemporary architecture examples found in the downtown and at the north of the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2015 BD Bacatá was inaugurated, surpassing the Colpatria Tower to become the tallest building of the city and of Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The building its expected to be the beginning of the city's downtown renovation.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_archives">Libraries and archives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Libraries and archives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007 Bogotá was named <a href="/wiki/World_Book_Capital" title="World Book Capital">World Book Capital</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Bogotá is the first Latin American city to receive this recognition, and the second one in the Americas after <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. It stood out in programs, the library network and the presence of organizations that, in a coordinated manner, are working to promote books and reading in the city. Several specific initiatives for the World Book Capital program have been undertaken with the commitment of groups, both public and private, engaged in the book sector.</p>
<p>The city is home to the Biblored, an institution which administers 16 small and four large public libraries (Biblioteca Virgilio Barco, Biblioteca El Tintal, Biblioteca El Tunal and Biblioteca Julio Mario Santodomingo). It also has six branches of the Library Network of the Family Compensation Fund Colsubsidio and libraries and documentation centers attached to institutions like the Museo Nacional de Colombia (specializing in old books, catalogs and art), Museum of Modern Art, the Alliance Française, and the Centro Colombo Americano.</p>
<p>Another set of libraries are the new collaborative initiatives between the state, city and international agencies. Examples are the Cultural Center Gabriel García Marquez, custom designed by the Fondo de Cultura Economica in Mexico, and the Spanish Cultural Center, which will begin construction with public funds and of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Government">Spanish Government</a> in downtown Bogotá.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Colombia" title="National Library of Colombia">National Library of Colombia</a> (1777), under the Ministry of Culture and the Biblioteca Luis Angel Arango (1958), under the Bank of the Republic are the two largest public libraries in the city. The first is the repository of more than two million volumes, with an important collection of ancient books. The latter has almost two million volumes. 45 thousand square meters in size, it hosts 10 thousand visitors a day. Bank of the Republic depends also on the Library Alfonso Palacio Rudas, north of the city, with about 50 thousand volumes. Other large public libraries are the Library of Congress in Colombia (with 100 thousand volumes), of the Instituto Caro y Cuervo (with nearly 200 thousand volumes, the largest Latin American library in Philology and Linguistics), the Library of the Academy of History The Library of the Academy of Language, the Library of the Colombian Institute of Anthropology and History ICANH, and many university libraries.</p>
<p>Bogotá is home to historical records housed in the General National Archive, a collection of about 60 million documents, one of the largest repositories of primary historical sources in Latin America. Bogotá is also home to the Musical Archive of the Cathedral of Bogotá (with thousands of books and choral song-colonial period), the Archdiocesan Archive, the Archive of the Conciliar Seminary of Bogotá, the Archive History National University of Colombia and the Archive of the Mint in Bogotá, under the Bank of the Republic.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_galleries">Museums and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Museums and galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG/220px-Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG/330px-Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG/440px-Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2748" data-file-height="3664" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
National Museum of Colombia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city offers 58 museums and over 70 art galleries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum" title="Colombian National Museum">Colombian National Museum</a> has acquisitions divided into four collections: art, history, archeology and ethnography. The <a href="/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Gold Museum, Bogotá">Gold Museum</a>, with 35,000 pieces of tumbaga gold, along with 30,000 objects in ceramic, stone and textiles, represents the largest collection of pre-Columbian gold in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Botero_Museum" title="Botero Museum">Botero Museum</a> has 123 works of Fernando Botero and 87 works by international artists. The Museum of Modern Art in Bogotá has a collection of graphic arts, industrial design and photography. The Museum of Colonial Art is home to an important collection of colonial art from Colombia. Fundación Gilberto Alzate Avendaño hosts activities related to the performing arts and shows temporary exhibits of art in its halls and galleries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Among the scientific museums are the Archeological Museum – Casa del Marqués de San Jorge, which has about 30 thousand pieces of pre-Columbian art, Instituto de Ciencias Naturales (UN), one of the four largest museums of natural sciences in Latin America, and the Geological Museum, which has a collection specializing in Geology and Paleontology.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Bogotá has historical museums like the <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Eliecer_Gaitan_Museum" title="Jorge Eliecer Gaitan Museum">Jorge Eliecer Gaitan Museum</a>, the Museum of Independence (Museo de la Independencia), the <a href="/wiki/Quinta_de_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Quinta de Bolívar">Quinta de Bolívar</a> and the Casa Museo Francisco José de Caldas, as well as the headquarters of Maloka and the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Children's Museum of Bogotá">Children's Museum of Bogotá</a>. New museums include the Art Deco and the Museum of Bogotá.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_arts">Theatre and arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Theatre and arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FITB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FITB.jpg/185px-FITB.jpg" width="185" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FITB.jpg/278px-FITB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FITB.jpg/370px-FITB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FITB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-American Theater Festival">Ibero-American Theater Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Picolontheaterj.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/af/Picolontheaterj.jpg/220px-Picolontheaterj.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/af/Picolontheaterj.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Picolontheaterj.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Teatro_de_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n" title="Teatro de Cristóbal Colón">Teatro de Cristóbal Colón</a></i> (Christopher Columbus Theater)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides the <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibero-American Theater Festival">Ibero-American Theater Festival</a>, the city has forty-five theaters; the principal ones are the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_de_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n" title="Teatro de Cristóbal Colón">Colon Theater</a>, the newly built <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biblioteca_P%C3%BAblica_Julio_Mario_Santo_Domingo" class="extiw" title="es:Biblioteca Pública Julio Mario Santo Domingo">Teatro Mayor Julio Mario Santo Domingo</a>, the National Theater with its two venues, the traditional TPB Hall, the Theater of La Candelaria, the Camarin del Carmen (over 400 years old, formerly a convent), the Colsubsidio, and a symbol of the city, the renovated <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teatro_Jorge_Eli%C3%A9cer_Gait%C3%A1n" class="extiw" title="es:Teatro Jorge Eliécer Gaitán">Teatro Jorge Eliecer Gaitan</a> (the highest capacity currently in South America), León de Greiff Auditorium (home of the Bogotá Philharmonic Orchestra), and the Open Air Theater "La Media Torta", where musical events are also held.</p>
<p>Bogotá has its own film festival, the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Film_Festival" title="Bogotá Film Festival">Bogotá Film Festival</a>, and many theatres, showing both contemporary films and art cinema.</p>
<p>The main cultural center of the city is the La Candelaria, historic center of the city, with a concentration of universities and museums. In 2007 Bogotá was designated the Ibero-American cultural Capital of Iberoamerica.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca" title="Spanish conquest of the Muisca">Spanish conquest</a>, the beliefs of the inhabitants of Bogotá formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_religion" title="Muisca religion">Muisca religion</a>. From the colonial period onwards, the city has been predominantly Roman Catholic. Proof of this religious tradition is the number of churches built in the historic city center. The city has been seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bogotá">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bogotá</a> since 22 March 1564. The seat of the Archbishop is the <a href="/wiki/Primary_Cathedral_of_Bogota" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary Cathedral of Bogota">Primary Cathedral of Bogota</a>; the archdiocese itself is located in new buildings in the north of the city. However a large group of the population nowadays declares itself non-practicing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The city has a mosque located in the area of Chapinero called the Estambul mosque,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> a mosque currently being built on the Calle 80 with Cra 30 called Abou Bakr Alsiddiq mosque<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> and which is the first in the city to have the traditional Islamic architecture, and an Islamic Center called Al-Qurtubi.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The main <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashkenazi">Ashkenazi</a> Jewish synagogue (there are a total of 4 synagogues in Bogotá) is located on 94th street (also called State of Israel avenue).</p>
<p>An Eastern Orthodox church and the San Pablo Anglican Cathedral, the mother church of the Episcopal Church in Colombia, are both located in Chapinero. The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Colombia_Temple" title="Bogotá Colombia Temple">Bogotá Colombia Temple</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> is located in the Niza neighborhood. There are four Buddhist centers located in the north of the city. There is also a wide variety of Protestant churches in different parts of the city, including the Bogotá Baptist Chapel, the non-denominational Union Church, and the St. Matthaus Evangelical Lutheran Church which holds services in German as well as Spanish for the German-Colombian community.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a broad array of restaurants in Bogotá that serve typical and international food. Parque de la 93, Usaquén, Zona T, The <a href="/w/index.php?title=G_Zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="G Zone (page does not exist)">G Zone</a>, La Macarena, La Candelaria and the International Centre are some of the main sectors where a number of international restaurants are found, ranging from Argentinian, Peruvian, Venezuelan, Brazilian, Mexican, American establishments to Arabic, Asian, French, Italian, Russian and British bistros, rotisseries, steakhouses and pubs, just to name a few. Typical dishes of Bogotá include the <a href="/wiki/Ajiaco" title="Ajiaco">Ajiaco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> a soup prepared with chicken, a variety of potatoes, corn on the cob, and <i><a href="/wiki/Galinsoga_parviflora" title="Galinsoga parviflora">guascas</a></i> (an herb), usually served with sour cream and capers, and accompanied by avocado and rice.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tamale" title="Tamale">Tamale</a> is a very traditional Bogotá dish. Colombian tamal is a paste made with rice, beef, pork and/or chicken (depending on the region), chickpea, carrot, and spices, wrapped in <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a> leaves and steam-cooked.</p>
<p>Figs with <a href="/wiki/Arequipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Arequipe">arequipe</a>, strawberries with cream, <i>postre de natas</i> and <i>cuajada con melao</i> are some of the main desserts offered in the city. <a href="/wiki/Canelazo" title="Canelazo">Canelazo</a> is a hot drink from the Altiplano prepared with <a href="/wiki/Aguapanela" title="Aguapanela">aguapanela</a>, cinnamon and <a href="/wiki/Aguardiente" title="Aguardiente">aguardiente</a>. Another hot beverage is the Carajillo, made with coffee (tinto as it is known in Colombia) and aguardiente.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">

</div>
</div>
</li>

</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are numerous parks in Bogotá, many with facilities for concerts, plays, movies, storytellers and other activities.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_Metropolitan_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Simón Bolívar Metropolitan Park">Simón Bolívar Metropolitan Park</a> is a large park regularly used to stage free concerts (such as the annual <a href="/wiki/Rock_al_parque" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock al parque">Rock al Parque</a>, a festival in which popular and/or recently formed international, latinamerican, and Colombian <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> bands play free of charge).</li>
<li>The public <i>Parque Nacional</i> (National Park) has green spaces, ponds, games for children, foot and bicycle paths, and venues for entertainment such as public screenings of movies and concerts and events organized by the Council of Bogotá</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Botanical_Garden" title="Bogotá Botanical Garden">Bogotá Botanical Garden</a> (<i>Jardín Botánico de Bogotá</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/93_Park" title="93 Park">Parque de la 93</a> has day-time leisure activities and nightlife. Several of the top restaurants and bars in the city are in this park, the park is known around the world like the Colombian <a href="/wiki/Pike_Place" class="mw-redirect" title="Pike Place">Pike Place</a> by having the first <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> in all the country and <a href="/wiki/Carls_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Carls Jr.">Carls Jr.</a> as well.</li>
<li>Mundo Aventura is an <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a>, with an entry charge and charges for the different attractions. It has rides for adults and children, a <a href="/wiki/Petting_zoo" title="Petting zoo">petting zoo</a>, and the "cerdodromo", where pigs race.</li>
<li>Salitre Mágico is another <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a> with rides and attractions. The park is near the Simón Bolívar park, where concerts are held throughout the year.</li>
<li>Parque del Chicó has trees, gardens, artificial creeks and ponds, and a colonial style house converted into a museum; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Museo_del_Chic%C3%B3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Museo del Chicó (page does not exist)">Museo del Chicó</a></li>
<li>To the north of Bogotá, in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Tocancip%C3%A1" title="Tocancipá">Tocancipá</a>; <a href="/wiki/Parque_Jaime_Duque" class="mw-redirect" title="Parque Jaime Duque">Parque Jaime Duque</a> has rides, a giant map of Colombia, popular exhibits, a zoo, and a big hand holding the world symbolizing God. There is a reproduction of the <a href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal" title="Taj Mahal">Taj Mahal</a> in the park with a collection of reproductions of famous paintings. The park is also used for large concerts, mainly electronic music ones.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maloka_Museum" title="Maloka Museum">Maloka</a> is an interactive museum of sciences</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Savannah_Railway" title="Bogotá Savannah Railway">Tourist train</a> is a sightseeing train, popular with Bogotá residents, which runs to outlying towns <a href="/wiki/Zipaquir%C3%A1" title="Zipaquirá">Zipaquirá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cajic%C3%A1" title="Cajicá">Cajicá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nemoc%C3%B3n" title="Nemocón">Nemocón</a> along the lines of the former <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Savannah_Railway" title="Bogotá Savannah Railway">Bogotá Savannah Railway</a> on weekends. The route to Zipaquirá (famous for its <a href="/wiki/Salt_Cathedral_of_Zipaquir%C3%A1" title="Salt Cathedral of Zipaquirá">salt cathedral</a>) is 53 kilometres (33 miles) long. Another line goes towards the north for 47&#160;km (29&#160;mi) and ends at <a href="/wiki/Brice%C3%B1o" title="Briceño">Briceño</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Usaqu%C3%A9n_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Usaquén Park (page does not exist)">Usaquén Park</a> is another of the most important parks in the city several of the best restaurants in this city are located there, is recognized to have street performers such as storytellers, magicians, jugglers, etc. and also for being one of the most decorated parks in the city during Christmas time.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U20_Bogota.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/U20_Bogota.jpg/220px-U20_Bogota.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/U20_Bogota.jpg/330px-U20_Bogota.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/U20_Bogota.jpg/440px-U20_Bogota.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U20_Bogota.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Estadio_El_Camp%C3%ADn" title="Estadio El Campín">Estadio El Campín</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The District Institute for Recreation and Sport promotes recreation, sports and use of the parks in Bogotá.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> has been declared a symbol of Bogotá, and is widely played in the city. There are three professional clubs in the city, <a href="/wiki/Club_Santa_Fe" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Santa Fe">Santa Fe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millonarios_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Millonarios Fútbol Club">Millonarios</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Equidad" title="La Equidad">La Equidad</a>. The main stadium in the city is The Campín Stadium (Estadio Nemesio Camacho El Campín) home of the local teams <a href="/wiki/Club_Santa_Fe" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Santa Fe">Santa Fe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millonarios" class="mw-redirect" title="Millonarios">Millonarios</a>, In 2001 The Campín Stadium has been the place for the <a href="/wiki/2001_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2001 Copa América">2001 Copa América</a> final between the <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia national football</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico national football</a>, final score 1-0 in favor of the home team and finally getting their first continental cup. The other soccer venue is the multi-use Techo Metropolitan Stadium which is the home of <a href="/wiki/La_Equidad" title="La Equidad">La Equidad</a>.</p>
<p>Other major sporting venues are the covered Coliseum El Campín, the Simón Bolívar Aquatic Complex, the Sports Palace, the El Salitre Sports Venue which includes the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carlos_Gal%C3%A1n_Velodrome" title="Luis Carlos Galán Velodrome">Luis Carlos Galán Velodrome</a> (which hosted the <a href="/wiki/1995_UCI_Track_Cycling_World_Championships" title="1995 UCI Track Cycling World Championships">1995 UCI Track Cycling World Championships</a>), the El Salitre Diamond Ballpark and the <a href="/wiki/BMX" title="BMX">BMX</a> track "Mario Andrés Soto".</p>
<p>Bogotá hosted the first Bolivarian Games held in 1938. The city hosted the National Games in 2004, winning the championship. It was a sub-venue Bolivarian Pan American Games. In addition, the city on the route of the Tour of Colombia.</p>
<p>After being a major venue city for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a> that was held in <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, the Colombian Football Federation announced that Bogotá will be one of the venue cities to host the <a href="/wiki/2016_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup" title="2016 FIFA Futsal World Cup">2016 FIFA Futsal World Cup</a> as well.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The flag originated with the insurgency movement against the colonial authorities which began on 20 July 1810, during which the rebels wore armbands with yellow and red bands, as these colours were those of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Spain" title="Flag of Spain">Spanish flag</a> used as the flag for the New Kingdom of Granada.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 9 October 1952, exactly 142 years after these events, decree 555 of 1952 officially adopted the patriotic armband as the flag of Bogotá.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The flag of Cundinamarca follows the same pattern, plus a light blue tile which represents the Virgin Mary's cape.</p>
<p>The flag itself is a yellow band above a red one. The yellow denotes the gold from the earth, as well as the virtues of justice, clemency, benevolence, the so-called "mundane qualities" (defined as nobility, excellence, richness, generosity, splendour, health, steadfastness, joy and prosperity), long life, eternity, power and constancy. The red denotes the virtue of charity, as well as the qualities of bravery, nobility, values, audacity, victory, honour and furor, Colombians call it the blood of their people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The coat of arms of the city was granted by emperor <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V (Charles I of Spain)</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a>, by royal decree given in <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, Spain on 3 December 1548. It contains a black eagle in the center, which symbolises steadfastness. The eagle is also a symbol of the Habsburgs, which was the ruling family of the Spanish empire at the time. The eagle is crowned with gold and holds a red pomegranate inside a golden background. The border contains olive branches with nine golden pomegranates on a blue background. The two red pomegranates symbolize audacity, and the nine golden ones represent the nine states which constituted the New Kingdom of Granada at the time. In 1932 the coat of arms was officially recognized and adopted as the symbol of Bogotá.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Bogotá's anthem lyrics were written by Pedro Medina Avendaño; the melody was composed by Roberto Pineda Duque. The song was officially declared the anthem by decree 1000 31 July 1974, by then Mayor of Bogotá, Aníbal Fernandez de Soto.</p>

</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bogotá is part of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities" title="Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</a><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> from 12 October 1982 establishing brotherly relations with the following cities:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra"><img alt="Andorra" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/22px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/33px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/43px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>, Andorra</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay"><img alt="Paraguay" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Paraguay.svg/23px-Flag_of_Paraguay.svg.png" width="23" height="13" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Paraguay.svg/35px-Flag_of_Paraguay.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Flag_of_Paraguay.svg/46px-Flag_of_Paraguay.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="330" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Asunci%C3%B3n" title="Asunción">Asunción</a>, Paraguay</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia"><img alt="Colombia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Colombia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Colombia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> Bogotá, Colombia</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina"><img alt="Argentina" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina</li>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala"><img alt="Guatemala" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Flag_of_Guatemala.svg/23px-Flag_of_Guatemala.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Flag_of_Guatemala.svg/35px-Flag_of_Guatemala.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Flag_of_Guatemala.svg/46px-Flag_of_Guatemala.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">Guatemala City</a>, Guatemala</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships_and_cooperations">Partnerships and cooperations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Partnerships and cooperations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other forms of cooperation and city friendship similar to the twin city programmes exist:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, Italy<sup id="cite_ref-Turin_twinnings_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turin_twinnings-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
